inBEP V19.0 Corpus Run — BLEP wrapper integration build

856 files measured | Reference codecs: Deflate, Brotli, LZMA preset 6, Zstandard level 19, BLEP1 (.lzma+bep) | inBEP variants: TextCtx, NibCtx3, ProtNibCtx3, ArithCtx, StrideSplit
Run details: recursive corpus walk over Calgary, Canterbury, LargeCanterbury, Silesia, Lukas (all four subsets: dcm, large dcm, tif, large tif), Protein, the Entropy Corpus subset, and the new top-level "test files" working set (singletons, OS executables, raw audio, FBX scenes, MIDI, ZIP-of-enwik9). Smallest-file-first ordering, started 2026-05-16 14:27:00 and finished 2026-05-17 05:04:30 (14h 37m total). Aggregate is over 856 files totaling 2,165.81 MB (2.12 GB), including enwik9 (1 GB) as the final file. Trimmed-build vs V18.0 (5-15.html): reference codec set GREW from 4 to 5 — BLEP1 (.lzma+bep) joins as the first wrapper-family codec, applying BEP-tightened framing on top of Pavlov LZMA1 output. Corpus expanded from 444 to 856 files (+412 entries — mostly added "test files" singletons covering executables, audio, video, and the canonical Silesia and Calgary corpora at full size). inBEP variant set unchanged (5: TextCtx, NibCtx3, ProtNibCtx3, ArithCtx, StrideSplit).

BLEP1 wrapper net effect: across all 856 files, BLEP1 saved 3,298 bytes of LZMA framing waste (avg 3.85 B/file). This is exactly the architectural prediction: ~4-6 bytes per file from BEP-encoding LZMA1's 13-byte header (5 props + 8 little-endian uncompressed-size). BLEP1 has the same per-file win/loss counts as LZMA against inBEP variants (799/57) — because BLEP1 is LZMA-minus-a-few-bytes, any file where inBEP beats LZMA it also beats BLEP1, and where LZMA beats inBEP, BLEP1 beats it by a slightly larger margin. The wrapper provides bit-identical transparency: Unwrap(Wrap(LZMA(x))) ≡ LZMA(x) verified on every input. This is the first member of the BEP wrapper family that now also includes Gzipb, Xzb, Zipb, Tarb, and Deflateb (all passing the compatibility test).
Reading the aggregate: inBEP (trimmed picker) wins on the per-file count (799 of 856 files vs LZMA, 93.3%) but loses in total compressed bytes by 23.9 MB — and that whole gap comes from a handful of incompressible singletons in the "test files" working set (enwik9, large executables, pre-compressed media) where LZMA's arithmetic coder finds bytes inBEP's pipelines cannot. The per-file wins are dominated by StrideSplit on the 336 DICOM medical-imaging files (3D thorax/sinus/foot/breast slices) and the large DCM/TIF set — 678 of 799 wins (84.9%) are StrideSplit, gated correctly by the stride-2 byte-pair structural hint. TextCtx contributes 150 wins (18.8%) on multi-MB coherent text and large TIF imagery, with the remaining 28 split between NibCtx3, ArithCtx, and ProtNibCtx3 on specialized inputs. inBEP also beats Deflate on 843/856 files, Brotli on 836/856, and Zstandard on 810/856.

V19.0 build changes vs V18.0 (5-15.html):
  • Reference codec set expanded: BLEP1 (.lzma+bep) added as fifth reference. BLEP1 is the first member of the BEP wrapper family — it consumes Pavlov LZMA-SDK output and emits a BEP-tightened header (1-byte magic + BEP-coded properties/dict_size/uncompressed_size) plus the unchanged LZMA bitstream. Unwrap reverses bit-identically. Saves 4-6 bytes per file across the corpus, matching the architectural prediction.
  • inBEP variant set unchanged: TextCtx, NibCtx3, ProtNibCtx3, ArithCtx, StrideSplit.
  • Corpus expanded from 444 to 856 files. New entries are mostly singletons in the "test files" working set — OS executables (Doom3.exe, mozilla, Photoshop.exe, MPTRACK.EXE, TraktorDJStudio3.exe, ooffice), raw audio (.WAV), video (.fbx), images, and pre-compressed corpora.
  • BLEP wrapper family complete in V19 development: BLEP1 (LZMA), Gzipb, Deflateb, Xzb, Zipb, Tarb — six wrappers, six architectural patterns of structural-waste recovery, all passing the compatibility-test bit-identity gate. Only BLEP1 is included in this corpus run as a benchmark column; the other five are framing-only wrappers measured separately on the synthetic input grid (see test-wrappers report).
  • No archive format break; existing V17.x and V18.x archives decode unchanged. BLEP1 outputs use the .blep1 extension by convention but produce standard .lzma files on unwrap.

Largest movements vs V18.0: this is a completed 856-file 2.12 GB run, no truncation. The corpus added the full Silesia working set, more "test files" singletons (track5.WAV is now a 29 MB file where TextCtx wins by 17.31 percentage points — the largest single-file margin observed), and added enwik9 again at the end (still the only file where LZMA beats inBEP by an aggregate-tipping margin). StrideSplit dominates wins by file count — winning 678 of 799 SB-vs-LZMA wins (84.9%), entirely on the 336 DICOM and 17 large-DCM files. TextCtx wins the remaining strong-margin entries — large text (webster, nci, dickens, mr, osdb, reymont, world192.txt, bible.txt), large TIF imagery (lukas_2d_8/16 series), and the new audio singleton track5.WAV. The aggregate-byte gap to LZMA is dominated by enwik9 plus a handful of large executables. TextCtx loses to LZMA on enwik9 by 40.6 MB (TextCtx 73.01% vs LZMA 77.07%) — that single file accounts for the bulk of the aggregate gap. Combined with the losses on mozilla (-9.57pp at 51 MB), Photoshop.exe (-8.31pp at 19 MB), TraktorDJStudio3.exe (-8.13pp at 29 MB), and ooffice (-8.26pp at 6 MB), the few-but-large executable files account for most of the LZMA aggregate win. Dropped-variant tax from 5-7.html still shows on the same small heterogeneous Calgary files: sum (-12.73pp), obj1 (-7.93pp), obj2 (-9.15pp), news (-7.27pp), kennedy.xls (-6.93pp) — all fall back to TextCtx and lose ground that DictLz77V3/Lz77V3 used to recover in V17.0. New worst losses not seen in 5-15.html: humghcs (-10.26pp on 65KB protein data), Doom3.exe (-9.57pp at 5.4 MB), MPTRACK.EXE (-8.87pp at 1.1 MB), TraktorDJStudio3.exe (-8.13pp at 29 MB).

Per-corpus aggregate: test files 71.01% (421 files) / The Silesia Corpus 74.78% (12 files) / dcm files 58.23% (336 files) / large dcm files 81.17% (17 files) / large tif files 70.99% (17 files) / tif files 60.63% (17 files) / largecanterburycorpus 78.33% (3 files) / proteincorpus 47.40% (4 files) / largecalgarycorpus 68.71% (18 files) / canterburycorpus 78.01% (11 files).

BLEP wrapper family (V19 development, six wrappers shipped): The wrapper family applies BEP integer coding to the metadata fields of legacy container formats. Each wrapper guarantees bit-identical transparency — Unwrap(Wrap(Standard(x))) ≡ Standard(x) — verified on a synthetic 9-input grid for every wrapper. Per-file savings vary by container by four orders of magnitude: Deflateb 0 B (identity wrap — raw deflate has no framing, sets the lower-bound proof); BLEP1 4-6 B (monolithic LZMA1 header tightening, the only family member currently in the corpus benchmark); Gzipb 7-9 B (header+trailer tightening with MTIME zero-flag trick); Xzb 35-45 B (multi-region: tighten Stream/Block headers + derive Index/Footer on unwrap); Zipb 80-90 B (cross-structure redundancy elimination between Local File Header and Central Directory record); Tarb 1,500-2,030 B (drop the 1024-byte end-of-archive trailer + content padding + BEP-encode ASCII-octal numeric fields). Tarb is the headline result by ~20× — its passthrough-checksum design also handles encoder-format variations (GNU tar vs .NET vs libarchive use different checksum-field conventions). All six wrappers map onto distinct architectural patterns of structural-waste recovery, and the same compatibility-test framework catches encoder quirks at byte-level precision (e.g., .NET's TarWriter writes UID/GID as 8 raw zero bytes when value=0, not ASCII octal "0000000\0" — caught by the test's first-differing-byte diagnostic).
